\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_calc_production_quantity}} \index{\url{Firm_calc_production_quantity}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firm calculate the intended production volume depending on the current stocks in the malls} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_set_quantities_zero}} \index{\url{Firm_set_quantities_zero}} & \parbox{10cm}{Dummy: no production on not\_day\_of\_month\_to\_act} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_calc_input_demands}} \index{\url{Firm_calc_input_demands}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firms calculate the labor demand and the demand for capital goods} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_calc_production_quantity_2}} \index{\url{Firm_calc_production_quantity_2}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firms iterate over the planned production quantity decreasing it incrementally,
 such that the corresponding labor demand and capital demand can be financed by 
 the actually obtained financial resources, AFTER all prior financial commitments have been paid.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_send_capital_demand}} \index{\url{Firm_send_capital_demand}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firm sends demand for capital to the capital goods market.} \\

\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_execute_production}} \index{\url{Firm_execute_production}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firm sends demand for capital to the capital goods market.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_calc_pay_costs}} \index{\url{Firm_calc_pay_costs}} & \parbox{10cm}{In this function the firm receives the purchased investment
 goods and pays the goods and   the wage bill. Additionally, the 
 new mean wage and the new average specific skill level is computed.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_send_goods_to_mall}} \index{\url{Firm_send_goods_to_mall}} & \parbox{10cm}{Here the firms send the produced goods to the malls. 
If the realized output is less than the intended one, then 
the malls are only delivered with a proportional 
share of their planned delivery volumes.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_calc_revenue}} \index{\url{Firm_calc_revenue}} & \parbox{10cm}{Here the firms calc the revenues and profits and then 
distribute the dividends to households.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{idle}} \index{\url{idle}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firm does nothing} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_compute_sales_statistics}} \index{\url{Firm_compute_sales_statistics}} & \parbox{10cm}{Here the firm computes the sales. This information is required for the production planning at the beginning of the next production cycle.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_update_specific_skills_of_workers}} \index{\url{Firm_update_specific_skills_of_workers}} & \parbox{10cm}{Because the specific skills of workers have changed the 
firms update the specific skill levels of the workers.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{idle}} \index{\url{idle}} & \parbox{10cm}{Firm does nothing} \\

\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{Firm_compute_financial_payments}} \index{\url{Firm_compute_financial_payments}} & \parbox{10cm}{Function to compute the prior financial commitments of the firm: interests, installments, taxes.} \\

 - production\_liquidity\_needs: to finance production costs: wage bill + capital investments} \\

The other applicants are refused.} \\

We only measure the 1-month survival rate: the percentage of firms age 0-59 months that are still active in the next month, thus having age 1-60 months.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{double} \url{survival_rate_multiperiod_1}} \index{\url{survival_rate_multiperiod_1}} & \parbox{10cm}{Multi-period survival rates. Definition: "The survival rate after x years is the percentage of all enterprise births of year n which are still active in year n+x." The 1st row survival\_rate\_multiperiod[0][.] equals survival\_rate[], and contains the 1-period survival rates (for all age bins 0-59). The 2nd row survival\_rate\_multiperiod[1][.] contains the 2-period survival rates (for all age bins 0-59), etc.} \\
\midrule

The 2nd row survival\_rate\_multiperiod[1][.] contains the 2-period survival rates (for all age bins 0-59), etc.} \\
\midrule
\parbox{5cm}{\url{double} \url{survival_rate_multiperiod}} \index{\url{survival_rate_multiperiod}} & \parbox{10cm}{Multi-period survival rates. \url{double} \url{debt_rescaling_factor} \index{\url{debt_rescaling_factor}} & \parbox{10cm}{The debt rescaling factor $\omega$ is used in case of a firm bankruptcy to rescale the debt. This is a process of debt-to-equity transformation. It sets the target debt level in relation to the value of total assets: $L^*=\omega A^*$. The firm will not refund all of its loans completely, but will write off every loan with a certain ratio: $w\_j = (1-L^*/L)L\_j$ for loan $j$. The fraction $(1-L^*/L)$ is the write-off ratio, and $w\_j$ is the monetary amount of the write-off for loan $j$.}\\
\url{double} \url{target_leverage_ratio} \index{\url{target_leverage_ratio}} & \parbox{10cm}{The target leverage ratio is the proportion of the target debt to target equity: $\ell = L^*/E^*$. This determines the target equity level as $E^*= (1/\ell) L^*$ and sets the amount of equity that the firm should raise on the financial market.}\\
\url{double} \url{target_liquidity_ratio} \index{\url{target_liquidity_ratio}} & \parbox{10cm}{The target liquidity ratio is a parameter used in the case of firm bankruptcy due to illiquidity. The amount of equity to raise on the AFM equals $\alpha (F-P)$, where $\alpha$ is the target liquidity ratio, F are the financial commitments, and P is the payment account.}\\
\url{double} \url{const_dividend_earnings_ratio} \index{\url{const_dividend_earnings_ratio}} & \parbox{10cm}{The parameter const\_dividend\_earnings\_ratio is used to determine the first positive dividend payment (if the dividend was set to 0, or at the start): TOTAL\_DIVIDEND\_PAYMENT = CONST\_DIVIDEND\_EARNINGS\_RATIO *NET\_EARNINGS;}\\
\url{double} \url{const_dividend_treshold_full_payout} \index{\url{const_dividend_treshold_full_payout}} & \parbox{10cm}{The parameter const\_dividend\_treshold\_full\_payout is used to set a treshold }\\
\url{int} \url{igfirm_dividend_payout_stretching_month} \index{\url{igfirm_dividend_payout_stretching_month}} & \parbox{10cm}{}\\
\url{double} \url{index_price_adj} \index{\url{index_price_adj}} & \parbox{10cm}{Lambda parameter in the (D/S)-price adjustment rule. Typical value: 1.0.}\\
\url{double} \url{index_price_adj_max} \index{\url{index_price_adj_max}} & \parbox{10cm}{Ceiling on price growth rate. Typical value: 1.10.}\\
\url{double} \url{index_price_adj_min} \index{\url{index_price_adj_min}} & \parbox{10cm}{Floor on negative price "growth" rate (the decrease rate). Typical value: 0.90.}\\
\url{int} \url{trading_activity} \index{\url{trading_activity}} & \parbox{10cm}{Flag to switch on/off the trading of index shares.

trading\_activity = 0: households receive dividends, but do not issue orders to re-adjust their asset portfolio.

trading\_activity = 1: households receive dividends, and issue orders to re-adjust their asset portfolio.}\\
\url{int} \url{trading_random} \index{\url{trading_random}} & \parbox{10cm}{Flag to switch on/off the random trading.
	}\\
